14313:1999.  ISO 14313 was prepared by Technical Committee ISO/TC 67  Materials, equipment and

document.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>Introduction<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This International Standard is based on API Specification 6D, twenty-first edition, March 1994.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Users of this International Standard should be aware that further or differing requirements may be needed for
individual applications. This International Standard is not intended to inhibit a vendor from offering, or the purchaser
from accepting, alternative equipment or engineering solutions for the individual application. This may be
particularly applicable where there is innovative or developing technology. Where an alternative is offered, the
vendor should identify any variations from this International Standard and provide details.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>American Petroleum Institute<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=1>>Petroleum and natural gas industries—
Pipeline transportation systems—Pipeline valves<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>1
Scope<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This International Standard specifies requirements and gives recommendations for the design, manufacturing,
testing and documentation of ball, check, gate and plug valves for application in pipeline systems meeting the
requirements of ISO 13623 for the petroleum and natural gas industries.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Valves for pressure ratings exceeding PN 420 (Class 2500) are not covered by this International Standard.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Annex A of this International Standard provides guidelines to assist the purchaser with valve type selection and
specification of specific requirements when ordering valves.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>2
Normative references<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The following normative documents contain provisions which, through reference in this text, constitute provisions of
this International Standard. For dated references, subsequent amendments to, or revisions of, any of these
publications do not apply. However, parties to agreements based on this International Standard are encouraged to
investigate the possibility of applying the most recent editions of the normative documents indicated below. For
undated references, the latest edition of the normative document referred to applies. Members of ISO and IEC
maintain registers of currently valid International Standards.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Non-International Standards may be replaced, by agreement, with other recognized and equivalent national or
industry standards.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

designation .<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

and designation.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>3
Terms and definitions<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For the purposes of this International Standard, the following terms and definitions apply:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.1
ANSI rating class
numerical pressure design class defined in ASME B16.5 and used for reference purposes<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
The ANSI rating class is designated by the word "Class" followed by a number.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.2
bi-directional valve
valve designed for blocking the fluid in both downstream and upstream directions<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.3
bleed
drain or vent<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.4
block valve
gate, plug or ball valve that blocks flow into the downstream conduit when in the closed position<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Valves are either single- or double-seated, bi-directional or uni-directional.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.5
breakaway thrust
breakaway torque
thrust or torque required for opening a valve with maximum pressure differential<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.6
by agreement
agreed between manufacturer and purchaser<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>3.7
double-block-and-bleed (DBB) valve
valve with two seating surfaces which, in the   closed position, blocks flow from both valve ends when the cavity
between the seating surfaces is vented through a bleed connection provided on the body cavity<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.8
drive train
all parts of a valve drive between the operator and the obturator, including the obturator but excluding the operator<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3<<HEADING_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>API Specification 6D/ISO 14313:1999
  American Petroleum Institute<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>3.9
flow coefficient
K v
volumetric flow rate, in cubic metres per hour, of water at a temperature between 5°C (40° F ) and 40°C (104° F)
passing through a valve and resulting in a pressure loss of 1 bar (14,7 psi)<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE     K v  relates to the flow coefficient  C v  in US gallons per minute at 15,6°C (60°F) resulting in a 1 psi pressure drop as
follows:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>K
C
v
v
=  1156
,<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.10
full-opening valve
valve with an unobstructed opening capable of allowing a sphere or other internal device for the same nominal size
as the valve to pass<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.11
handwheel
wheel consisting of a rim connected to a hub, for example, by spokes, and used to operate manually a valve
requiring multiple turns<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.12
locking device
part or an arrangement of parts for securing a valve in the open and/or closed position<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.13
manual actuator
manual operator
wrench (lever) or handwheel with or without a gearbox<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.14
maximum pressure differential (MPD)
maximum difference between the upstream and downstream pressure across the obturator at which the obturator
may be operated<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.15
nominal pipe size (NPS)
numerical inches designation of size which is common to components in piping systems of any one size<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>NOTE
The nominal pipe size is   designated by the letters NPS followed by a number.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.16
nominal pressure (PN) class
numerical pressure design class as defined in ISO 7005-1 and used for reference purposes<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE  The nominal pressure (PN) class is designated by the abbreviation PN followed by a number.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.17
nominal size (DN)
numerical metric designation of size which is common to components in piping systems of any one size<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Nominal size is designated by the letters DN followed by a number.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.18
obturator
closure member
part of a valve, such as a ball, clapper, disc, gate or plug, which is positioned in the flow stream to permit or block
flow<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.19
operator
device (or assembly) for opening or closing a valve<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>4<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>TIPVALVE   Tel:+86-577-88732275  Fax:+86-577-88732276  E-mail:sales@tipvalve.com<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_12>>
<<HEADING level=3>>  American Petroleum Institute
API Specification 6D/ISO 14313:1999<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.20
position indicator
device to show the position of the valve obturator<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.21
powered actuator
powered operator
electric, hydraulic or pneumatic device bolted or otherwise attached to the valve for powered opening and closing of
the valve<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.22
pressure class
numerical pressure design class expressed in accordance with either the nominal pressure (PN) class or the ANSI
rating class<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
In this International Standard, the pressure class is stated by the PN class followed by the ANSI rating class between
brackets.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.23
pressure-containing parts
parts, such as bodies, bonnets, glands, stems, gaskets and bolting, designed to contain the pipeline fluid<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.24
pressure-controlling parts
parts, such as seat and obturator, intended to block or permit the flow of fluids<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.25
process-wetted parts
parts exposed directly to the pipeline fluid<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.26
reduced-opening valve
valve with the opening through the obturator smaller than at the end connection(s)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.27
seating surfaces
contact surfaces of the obturator and seat which ensure valve sealing<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.28
stem
part that connects the obturator to the operator and which may consist of one or more components<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.29
stem extension assembly
assembly consisting of the stem extension and the stem extension housing<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.30
support ribs or legs
metal structure which provides a stable footing when the valve is set on a fixed base<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.31
through-conduit valve
valve with an unobstructed and continuous cylindrical opening<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.32
twin-seat, both seats   bi-directional, valve
valve with two seats, each sealing in both directions<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5<<HEADING_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>3.33
twin-seat, one seat uni-directional and one seat bi-directional, valve
valve with two seats, one sealing in one direction and the other in either direction<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.34
uni-directional valve
valve designed for blocking the flow in one direction only<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>3.35
venturi plug valve
valve with a substantially reduced opening through the plug and a smooth transition from each full-opening end to
the reduced opening<<HEADING_END>>

API Specification 6D/ISO 14313:1999<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5
Valve types and configurations<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.1
Valve types<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.1.1
Gate valves<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Typical configurations for gate valves with flanged and welding ends are shown, for illustration purposes only, in
Figures 1 and 2.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Gate valves shall have an obturator which moves in a plane perpendicular to the direction of flow. The gate can be
constructed of one piece for slab-gate valves or of two or more pieces for expanding-gate valves.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Gate valves shall be provided with a back seat or secondary stem sealing feature in addition to the primary stem
seal.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.1.2
Lubricated and non-lubricated plug valves<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Typical configurations for plug valves with flanged and welding ends are shown, for illustration purposes only, in
Figure 3 .<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Plug valves shall have a cylindrical or conical obturator which rotates about an axis perpendicular to the direction of
flow.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.1.3
Ball valves<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Typical configurations for ball valves with flanged or welding ends are shown, for illustration purposes only, in
Figures 4, 5 and 6.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Ball valves shall have a spherical obturator which rotates on an axis perpendicular to the direction of flow.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.1.4
Check valves<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Typical configurations for check valves are shown, for illustration purposes only, in Figures 7 to 11. Check valves
may also be of the wafer type.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Check valves shall have an obturator which responds automatically to block fluid in one direction.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.2
Valve configurations<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.2.1
Full-opening valves<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Full-opening valves shall be unobstructed in the fully opened position and have an internal bore as specified in
Table 1. There is no restriction on the upper limit of valve bore sizes.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Full-opening through-conduit valves shall have a circular bore in the obturator that will allow a sphere with a nominal
size not less than that specified in Table 1 to pass.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Welding-end valves may require a smaller bore at the welding end to mate with the pipe.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>5.2.2
Reduced-opening valves<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The internal bore of reduced-opening valves shall be less than the internal bore specified in Table 1.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>TIPVALVE   Tel:+86-577-88732275  Fax:+86-577-88732276  E-mail:sales@tipvalve.com<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>Figure 11—Single-plate wafer-type check valve, short pattern<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6
Design<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.1
Pressure and temperature rating<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The nominal pressure (PN) class or the ANSI rating class shall be used for the specification of the required
pressure class.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Valves covered by this International Standard should be furnished in one of the following classes:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>PN 20 (Class 150)
PN 150 (Class 900)<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>PN 50 (Class 300)
PN 250 (Class 1500)<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>PN 64 (Class 400)
PN 420 (Class 2500)<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>PN 100 (Class 600)<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Pressure classes shall be specified by the purchaser in accordance with the applicable rating tables for material
groups in ASME B16.34.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The purchaser may specify intermediate design pressures and temperatures for his specific application.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Allowable operating pressures and temperatures for valves made of materials not covered by ASME B16.34 shall
be determined by calculations in accordance with an agreed pressure vessel design standard, such as ASME
Section VIII, Division 1 and Division 2, or BS 5500.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Non-metallic parts may limit minimum and maximum operating pressures and temperatures.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The maximum operating pressure at the minimum and maximum operating temperatures shall be marked on the
nameplate.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>19<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>TIPVALVE   Tel:+86-577-88732275  Fax:+86-577-88732276  E-mail:sales@tipvalve.com<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_27>>
<<HEADING level=3>>API Specification 6D/ISO 14313:1999
  American Petroleum Institute<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.2
Sizes<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>All valves, except for reduced-opening valves, shall be furnished in the nominal sizes (DN) listed in Tables 2 to 6.
Reduced-opening valves shall be furnished in the nominal sizes in accordance with Table 1.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE  In this International Standard, DN sizes are stated first followed by the equivalent NPS size between brackets.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Except for reduced-opening valves, valve sizes shall be specified   by the nominal sizes (DN) or nominal pipe size
(NPS).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Reduced-opening valves with a circular opening through the obturator shall be specified by the nominal size of the
end connections and the nominal size of the minimum bore of the obturator in accordance with Table 1, except that
for valve sizes DN 50 (NPS 2) or smaller the actual bore of the obturator shall be specified. For example, a DN 400
valve with a reduced 334-mm-diameter circular opening through the obturator shall be specified as 400  ×  350.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Reduced-opening valves with a non-circular opening through the obturator and reduced-opening check valves shall
be designated as reduced-bore valves and specified by the nominal size corresponding to the end connections
followed by the letter "R". For example, a reduced-bore valve with DN 400 end connections and a 381  ×  305 mm
rectangular opening through the obturator shall be specified as 400R.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.3
Face-to-face and end-to-end dimensions<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Unless otherwise agreed, face-to-face and end-to-end dimensions of valves shall be in accordance with Tables
2 to 6.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Face-to-face and end-to-end dimensions for valve sizes not specified in Tables 2 to 6 shall be in accordance with
ASME B16.10. Face-to-face and end-to-end dimensions not shown in Tables 2 to 6 or in ASME B16.10 shall be
established by agreement.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The length of valves having one welding end and one flanged end shall be determined by adding half the length of a
flanged-end valve to half the length of a welding-end valve.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Tolerances on the face-to-face and end-to-end dimensions shall be  ±   2 mm for valve sizes DN 250 and smaller, and
±   3 mm for valve sizes DN 300 and larger.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The nominal size and face-to-face or end-to-end dimensions shall be stated on the nameplate if not specified in or
not in accordance with Tables 2 to 6.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>6.4
Minimum-bore full-opening valves<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Minimum bores for full-opening valves shall not be less than those specified in Table 1.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.5
Valve operation<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The purchaser should specify the maximum pressure differential (MPD) at which the valve is required to be opened
by the lever, gearbox or actuator. If not specified, the pressure rating as determined in accordance with 6.1 for
material at 38°C (100°F) shall be the MPD.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The manufacturer shall provide the following data to the purchaser:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   the flow coefficient  K v ;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   the breakaway thrust or torque for new valve;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   the maximum allowable stem thrust or torque on the valve and, if applicable, the drive train.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.6
Pigging<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The purchaser shall specify the requirements for piggability of the valves. Clause A.4 may be used to assist.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>API Specification 6D/ISO 14313:1999

<<HEADING level=3>>6.7
Valve ends<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.7.1
Flanged ends<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Standard end flanges shall be furnished with a raised face or ring joint faces (raised face or full face). Dimensions,
tolerances and finishes, including drilling templates, flange facing, spot facing and back facing, shall be in
accordance with:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   ASME B16.5 for sizes up to and including DN 600 (NPS 24), except DN 550 (NPS 22);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   MSS SP-44 for DN 550 (NPS 22);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   ASME B16.47 Series A for DN 650 (NPS 26) and larger sizes.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.7.2
Welding ends<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Welding ends shall conform to Figures 434.86 (a) (1) and (2) of ASME B31.4 or Figures 14 and 15 of ASME B31.8
unless otherwise agreed. In the case of a heavy-wall valve body, the outside profile may be tapered at 30° and then
to 45° as illustrated in Figure 1 of ASME B16.25.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The purchaser shall specify the outside diameter, wall thickness, material grade, SMYS and special chemistry of the
mating pipe, and whether cladding has been applied.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.7.3
Special flanges and mechanical joints<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Other end connections, such as special flanges or mechanical joints, may be specified by the purchaser.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.8
Pressure relief<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The manufacturer shall determine whether fluid can become trapped in the body cavity in the open- and/or closed-
valve position.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If fluid trapping is possible, then valves for gas service, unless otherwise specified by the purchaser, and liquid
service shall be provided with an automatic cavity pressure relief.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Cavity relief, when required, shall prevent the pressure in the cavity from exceeding 1,33 times the valve pressure
rating determined in accordance with 6.1 for material at 38°C (100°F). External cavity relief valves shall be DN 15
(N PS  1 / 2 ) or larger.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>--``-`-`,,`,,`,`,,`---<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.9
Bypass, drain and vent connections<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Bypass, drain and vent connections and plug entries shall be drilled and threaded unless otherwise specified. The
purchaser may specify other types of connections, such as welded or flanged.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Threads shall be either tapered and capable of providing a pressure-tight seal or parallel-threaded. Connections or
plugs with parallel threads shall have a head section for trapping and retaining a sealing member suitable for the
specified valve service.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Thread sizes shall be in accordance with Table 7. Thread forms shall be in accordance with ASME B1.1,
ASME B1.20.1, ISO 228-1, ISO 228-2 or ISO 7-1.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>34<<HEADING_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>6.10
Handwheels and wrenches (levers)<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Wrenches for valves shall either be of an integral design or consist of a head which fits on the stem and is designed
to take an extended handle. The head design shall allow permanent attachment of the extended section if specified
by the purchaser.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The maximum force required at the handwheel or wrench to apply the breakaway torque or thrust shall not exceed
360 N.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Wrenches shall not be longer than twice the face-to-face or end-to-end dimension of the valve.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Handwheel diameter(s) shall not exceed the face-to-face or end-to-end length of the valve or 1   000 mm, whichever
is the smaller, unless otherwise agreed. Except for valve sizes DN 40 (NPS 1 1 / 2 ) and smaller, spokes shall not
extend beyond the perimeter of the handwheel unless otherwise agreed.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>When specified by the purchaser, the handwheel of the gearbox input shaft shall be provided with a torque-limiting
device, such as a shear pin, to prevent damage to the drive train.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.11
Locking devices<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Valves shall be supplied with locking devices if specified by the purchaser. Locking devices for check valves shall
be designed to lock the valve in the open position only.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Locking devices for other types of valve shall be designed to lock the valve in the open and/or closed position.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.12
Position indicators<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Valves fitted with manual or powered actuators shall be furnished with a visible indicator to show the open and the
closed position of the obturator.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For plug and ball valves, the wrench and/or the position indicator shall be in line with the pipeline when the valve is
open and transverse when the valve is closed. The design shall be such that the component(s) of the indicator
and/or wrench cannot be assembled to falsely indicate the valve position.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Valves without position stops shall have provision for the verification of open and close alignment with the
operator/actuator removed .<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>API Specification 6D/ISO 14313:1999
  American Petroleum Institute<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.13
Operators and stem extensions<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.13.1 Misalignment<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Misalignment or improper assembly of components shall be prevented by suitable means, such as a dowel pin or
fitting bolt, which ensure the unique location of manual or powered operators and stem extension assemblies.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.13.2 Sealing<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>External connections shall be sealed, for example with gaskets or O-rings, to prevent external contaminants
entering the mechanism.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.13.3 Overpressure protection<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Operators and stem extension assemblies shall be provided with a means of preventing pressure build-up in the
mechanism resulting from stem or bonnet seal leakage.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.14
Sealant injection<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Seat and/or stem sealant injection shall be provided when specified.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.15
Lifting lugs<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Valves of size DN 200 (NPS 8) and larger shall be provided with lifting lugs.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.16
Actuators<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Actuators may be powered by electric, hydraulic or pneumatic means.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The interface between actuators and valve bonnet or stem extension assemblies shall be designed to prevent
misalignment or improper assembly of the components.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The interface between actuators and valve bonnet or stem extension assemblies shall be sealed with gaskets or
O-rings to prevent external contaminants from entering the assembly.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Means shall be provided of preventing pressure build-up in the actuator from stem or bonnet seal leakage.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The output of the actuator shall not exceed the maximum load capacity of the valve drive train.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Typical valve-to-actuator interfaces are given in ISO 5211.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.17
Drive trains<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.17.1 Design thrust or torque<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The design thrust or torque for all drive train calculations shall be at least two times the breakaway thrust or torque.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE   This factor of safety is to allow for thrust or torque increase in service due to infrequent cycling, low-temperature
operation and the adverse effect of debris.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.17.2 Allowable stresses<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Tensile stresses in drive train components, including stem extensions, shall not exceed 67% of SMYS when
delivering the design thrust or torque. Shear, torsion and bearing stresses shall not exceed the limits specified in
ASME Code Section VIII, Division 2, Part AD-132.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>A strength efficiency factor of 0,75 shall be used for fillet welds.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>36<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>TIPVALVE   Tel:+86-577-88732275  Fax:+86-577-88732276  E-mail:sales@tipvalve.com<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_44>>
<<HEADING level=3>>  American Petroleum Institute
API Specification 6D/ISO 14313:1999<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.17.3 Allowable deflections<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For ball valves, the total torsional deflection of the extended drive train when delivering the design torque shall not
exceed the overlap contact angle between the seat and obturator.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Deflections of the extended drive train shall not prevent the obturator from reaching the fully closed position.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.18
Stem retention<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Valves shall be designed with a stem anti-blow-out device to prevent stem ejection by internal pressure when the
stem packing and/or retainer has been removed.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.19
Fire safety<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If specified by the purchaser, fire resistance certification of the design shall be provided, in accordance with clause A.5.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.20
Anti-static device<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>If specified by the purchaser, valves shall be provided with an anti-static device and tested in accordance with
clause C.5.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.21
Design documents<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The design shall be documented in a retrievable and reproducible form.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>6.22
Design document review<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Design documentation shall be reviewed and verified by competent personnel other than the person who performed
the original design.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7
Materials<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.1
Material specification<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Materials shall be procured to documented specifications.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Specifications for metallic parts shall, as a minimum, specify the requirements for:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   chemical properties;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   heat treatment;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   mechanical properties;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   testing;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   certification.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Metallic pressure-containing parts, except stems and gaskets, shall be made of materials listed in ASME B16.34 or,
by agreement, an equivalent standard.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.2
Service compatibility<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>All process-wetted parts, metallic and non-metallic, and lubricants shall be suitable for the commissioning fluids and
service specified by the purchaser.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Non-metallic parts of valves intended for hydrocarbon gas service at pressures of PN 100 (Class 600) or above
shall be resistant to explosive decompression.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>TIPVALVE   Tel:+86-577-88732275  Fax:+86-577-88732276  E-mail:sales@tipvalve.com<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_45>>
<<HEADING level=3>>API Specification 6D/ISO 14313:1999
  American Petroleum Institute<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.3
Forged parts<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Forged pressure-containing parts shall be forged close to the finished shape and size.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.4
Welding ends<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The chemistry of carbon steel welding ends shall meet the following requirements:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) The carbon content shall not exceed 0,23% by mass in the ladle (heat) analysis or 0,25% by mass in the
product (check) analysis.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) The maximum content of both sulfur and phosphorus shall not exceed 0,035% by mass.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) The carbon equivalent (CE) shall not exceed 0,43 in the ladle (heat) analysis or 0,45 in the product (check)
analysis. The CE shall be calculated in accordance with the following formula:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>CE = % C + (% Mn/6) + (% Cr + % Mo + % V)/5 + (% Ni + % Cu)/15<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The chemistry of austenitic stainless steels for welding ends shall meet the following requirements:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) The carbon content shall not exceed 0,03% by mass, except under the conditions outlined in b) and c) below.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) A carbon content of up to 0,08% by mass is permissible provided the material is stablized with niobium and the
niobium content is at least 10 times the carbon content by mass.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) For steels stabilized with niobium or tantalum, the combined mass of niobium and tantalum shall be at least
eight times the mass of the carbon.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Requirements for the chemistry of welding ends made of other materials shall be established by agreement.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>7.5
Toughness test requirements<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>All carbon and low-alloy steels for pressure-containing parts in valves with a specified design temperature below
−   29°C ( −   20°F) shall be impact-tested using the Charpy V-notch technique in accordance with ISO 148 or
ASTM A 370.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Design standards/codes or local requirements may require impact testing for minimum design temperatures higher
than  −   29°C ( −   20°F).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>A minimum of one impact test, comprising a set of three specimens, shall be performed on a representative test bar
of each heat of the material in the final heat-treated condition.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Test specimens shall be cut from a separate or attached block taken from the same heat, reduced by forging where
applicable, and heat-treated in the same heat treatment batch, including stress-relieving, as the product materials
except that:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   pressure-containing parts stress-relieved at or below a previous stress-relieving or tempering temperature need
not be retested;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   retesting is not required after stress-relieving if the measured toughness of the material before stress-relieving
is three times the required toughness.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Toughness testing may be performed during the qualification of the valve manufacturing procedure provided that
the material for testing is heat-treated using the same equipment as during valve production.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The impact test temperature shall be as defined in the applicable material specifications and pipeline design
standard/code.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Except for material for bolting, impact test results for full-size specimens shall meet the requirements of Table 8.
Impact test results for bolting material shall meet the requirements of ASTM A 320.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>7.6
Bolting<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Bolting shall be suitable for the specified valve service and pressure rating.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Bolting material with a mechanical strength above ASTM A 193 Grade B7 or hardness exceeding HRC22 shall not
be used for valve applications where hydrogen embrittlement may occur, unless otherwise agreed. For example,
hydrogen embrittlement can occur in buried pipelines with cathodic protection.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>8
Welding<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8.1
Qualifications<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Welding, including repair welding, of pressure-containing and pressure-controlling parts shall be performed in
accordance with procedures qualified to ASME Section IX or EN 288 − 3, and 8.2 and 8.3 of this International
Standard. Welders and welding operators shall be qualified in accordance with ASME Section IX or EN 287 − 1.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
The purchaser, pipeline design standards/codes, material specifications and local requirements may specify
additional requirements.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The results of all qualification tests shall be documented in a procedure qualification record (PQR).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Post-weld heat treatment (PWHT) shall be performed in accordance with the relevant material specification.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Some pipeline-welding standards, such as BS 4515, may have more stringent requirements for the essential
variables of welding. It may be necessary to provide full weld test rings, in the same heat treatment condition as the finished
valve, for weld procedure qualification.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>8.2
Impact testing<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Impact testing shall be carried out for the qualification of procedures for welding on valves with a design
temperature below  −   29°C ( −   20°F).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
Design code and/or local requirements may require impact testing at minimum design temperatures above  −   29°C
( −   20°F).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>A set of three weld metal impact specimens shall be taken from the weld metal (WM) at the location shown in
Figure 12. The specimens shall be oriented with the notch perpendicular to the surface of the material.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>A set of three impact specimens shall be taken from the heat-affected zone (HAZ) at the location shown in
Figure 13. The notch shall be placed perpendicularly to the material surface at a location resulting in a maximum
amount of HAZ material located in the resulting fracture.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>9.2
Measuring and test equipment<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.2.1
General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Equipment used to inspect, test or examine material or equipment shall be identified, controlled and calibrated at
intervals specified in the manufacturer’s instructions.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.2.2
Dimension-measuring equipment<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Equipment for measuring dimensions shall be controlled and calibrated in accordance with methods specified in
documented procedures.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.2.3
Pressure-measuring devices<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.2.3.1 Type and accuracy<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Test pressure measuring devices shall be either pressure gauges or pressure transducers which are accurate to
within  ±    2,0% of the full-scale reading.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.2.3.2 Gauge range<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Pressure measurements shall be made between 25% and 75% of the full pressure range of the measuring device.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.2.3.3 Calibration procedure<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Pressure-measuring devices shall be periodically recalibrated with a master pressure-measuring device or a
deadweight tester at 25%, 50%, 75% and 100% of the full pressure scale.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.2.4
Temperature-measuring devices<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Devices for measuring temperature, if required, shall be capable of indicating and recording temperature
fluctuations of 3°C (5°F).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.3
Qualification of inspection and test personnel<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.3.1
NDE personnel<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NDE personnel shall be qualified in accordance with the requirements specified in ASNT SNT-TC-1A or EN 473
Level II as a minimum .<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Personnel performing visual examinations shall have passed an annual eye examination in accordance with
ASNT SNT-TC-1A or EN 473 within the previous twelve months.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.3.2
Welding inspectors<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Personnel performing visual inspection of welding operations and completed welds shall be qualified and certified to
the requirements of AWS QC1, or equivalent, or a manufacturer’s documented training programme.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>9.4
NDE of repair welding<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>After defect removal, the excavated area shall be examined by magnetic particle (MT) or liquid penetrant (PT)
methods prior to starting repair welding.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Repair welds on pressure-containing parts shall be examined using MT or PT methods. Acceptance criteria shall be
specified in documented procedures.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The supplementary NDE requirements in Annex B, if specified by the purchaser, shall also apply to repair welding.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>10
Pressure testing<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10.1
General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Each valve shall be tested in accordance with this clause prior to shipment. The purchaser shall specify which
particular supplementary tests in Annex C shall be performed, together with the frequency of testing.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Testing shall be performed in the sequence used in this clause for specifying the test requirements. Shell pressure
testing shall be carried out before painting of the valves.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Test fluids shall be fresh water which may contain a corrosion inhibitor and, by agreement, antifreeze. The chloride
content of test water for austenitic and ferritic-austenitic (duplex) stainless-steel body/bonnet valves shall not
exceed 30  µ g/g (30 ppm).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Valves shall be tested with the seating and sealing surfaces free from sealant except where the sealant is the
primary means of sealing.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Tests specified with the valve half-open may also be performed with the valve fully open provided the body cavity is
simultaneously filled and pressurized through a cavity connection.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Methods for monitoring pressures and/or leakage shall be adequate also when valve body connections are not
available for direct monitoring.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>A sufficient stabilization period shall be allowed for all pressure tests.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Pressure testing shall be performed in accordance with documented procedures.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10.2
Stem backseat test<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Unless otherwise agreed, stem backseat testing shall be performed prior to shell testing.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Where a valve has a stem backseat feature, testing of the backseat shall commence with the seat free. Self-
energized packing or seals shall be removed unless a test port is provided for this test.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The valves shall be filled with the ends closed off and the obturator in the partially open position until leakage of the
test fluid around the stem is observed. The backseat shall then be closed and a minimum pressure of 1,1 times the
pressure rating determined in accordance with 6.1 for material at 38°C (100°F) is applied for the duration specified
in Table 9.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Monitoring for leakage shall be through a test access port or by monitoring leakage around the loosened packing.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>No visible leakage is permitted at this test pressure.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>10.3
Hydrostatic shell test<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Hydrostatic shell testing shall be performed on the fully assembled valve prior to painting.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Valves shall be closed off and the obturator placed in the partially open position during the test. If specified by the
purchaser, the method of closing the ends shall permit the transmission of the full-pressure force acting on the end
blanks to the valve body. Where present, external relief valves shall be removed and their connections plugged.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The test pressure shall be 1,5 or more times the pressure rating determined in accordance with 6.1 for material at
38°C (100°F). The duration shall not be less than that specified in Table 10.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>10.4.4 Acceptance criteria<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Leakage for soft-seated valves and lubricated plug valves shall not exceed ISO 5208 Rate A (no visible leakage).
For metal-seated valves the leakage rate shall not exceed ISO 5208 Rate D, except that the leakage rate during the
seat test in 10.4.5.5.2 shall not be more than two times ISO 5208 Rate D unless otherwise specified. The test
procedures for various types of block valve are given in 10.4.5.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10.4.5 Test procedures for block valves<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10.4.5.1 Uni-directional<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>With the valve half-open, the valve and its cavity shall be completely filled with test fluid. The valve shall then be
closed and the test pressure applied to the appropriate end of the valve.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Leakage from each seat shall be monitored via the valve body cavity vent or drain connection. For valves without a
body cavity connection, seat leakage shall be monitored from each seat at the respective downstream end of the
valve (the valve end downstream of the pressurized test fluid).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10.4.5.2 Bi-directional<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>With the valve half-open, the valve and its cavity shall be completely filled with test fluid. The valve shall then be
closed and the test pressure applied successively to both ends of the valve.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Seat leakage shall be monitored from each seat via the valve body cavity vent or drain connection. For valves
without a body cavity vent or drain connection, seat leakage shall be monitored from the respective downstream
end of the valve.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10.4.5.3 Twin-seat, both seats bi-directional<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Each seat shall be tested in both directions.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Cavity relief valves shall be removed if fitted. The valve and cavity shall be filled with test fluid, with the valve half-
open, until the test fluid overflows through the cavity relief connection.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>To test for seat leakage in the direction of the cavity, the valve shall be closed. The test pressure shall be applied
successively to each valve end to test each seat separately from the upstream side. Leakage shall be monitored via
the valve cavity pressure relief connection.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Thereafter, each seat shall be tested as a downstream seat. Both ends of the valve shall be drained and the valve
cavity filled with test fluid. Pressure shall then be applied whilst monitoring leakage through each seat at both ends
of the valve.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10.4.5.4 Twin-seat, one seat uni-directional and one seat bi-directional<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10.4.5.4.1
Uni-directional seat<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>With the valve half-open, the valve and the test cavity shall be completely filled with test fluid until fluid overflows
though the valve cavity vent connection. The valve shall then be closed and the vent valve on the test closure
opened to allow fluid to overflow, or the test closure on the downstream end of the valve removed. The test
pressure shall then be applied to the upstream end (uni-directional seat end) and leakage monitored from the cavity
connection. If leakage is also occurring through the downstream seat, the upstream seat leakage shall be taken as
the sum of the leakage measured from the cavity and the downstream connections.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>45<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>TIPVALVE   Tel:+86-577-88732275  Fax:+86-577-88732276  E-mail:sales@tipvalve.com<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

| Valve size   |          | Test duration   |
|              |          | (minutes)       |
|:-------------|:---------|:----------------|
| DN           | NPS      |                 |
| (mm)         | (inches) |                 |
| 15 – 100     | 1/2 – 4  | 2               |
| ≥ 150        | ≥ 6      | 5               |

<<PAGE_53>>
<<HEADING level=3>>API Specification 6D/ISO 14313:1999
  American Petroleum Institute<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10.4.5.4.2
Bi-directional seat<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The test in 10.4.5.4.1 shall be repeated to test the bi-directional seat in its upstream-sealing direction.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>To test the bi-directional seat in its downstream-sealing direction, both ends of the valve shall be blanked off. With
the valve half-open, the valve shall be completely filled with test fluid and pressurized to the test pressure. The valve
shall then be closed and test fluid allowed to overflow from a connection on the test closure fitted to the end of the
valve at the bi-directional seat end (i.e., downstream of the bi-directional seat). The test pressure shall be
maintained on the cavity connection whilst monitoring seat leakage of the bi-directional seat at the overflow
connection on the downstream test closure.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10.4.5.5 Double-block-and-bleed valves<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10.4.5.5.1
Single-seat test<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>With the valve half-open, the valve and its cavity shall be completely filled with test fluid. The valve shall then be
closed and the valve body vent valve opened to allow excess test fluid to overflow from the valve cavity test
connection. The test pressure shall then be applied to one end of the valve and the pressure released at the other
end. This test shall be repeated for the other valve end.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Seat tightness shall be monitored during each test via overflow from the valve cavity connection.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10.4.5.5.2
Double-block seat test<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>With the valve half-open, the valve and its cavity shall be completely filled with test fluid. The valve shall then be
closed and the valve body vent valve opened to allow excess test fluid to overflow from the valve cavity test
connection. The test pressure shall be applied simultaneously from both valve ends.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Seat tightness shall be monitored via overflow through the valve cavity connection.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The tests in 10.4.5.5 may be performed in any order by the manufacturer.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10.4.5.6 Check valves<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The pressure shall be applied in the direction of the required flow blockage.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10.4.5.7 Installation of body connections after testing<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Pressure-containing parts, such as vent/or drain plug(s) and cavity relief valves, shall be fitted, on completion of
testing, in accordance with documented procedures.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>10.5
Draining<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Valves shall be drained of test fluids and, where applicable, lubricated before shipment.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>11
Marking<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>11.1
Requirements<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Valves shall be marked in accordance with Table 12.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>On valves whose size or shape limits the body markings, they may be omitted in the following order:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   size;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   rating;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   material;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   manufacturer’s name or trademark.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The nameplate and serial number may be omitted for valves smaller than DN 50 (NPS 2). The purchaser may
specify requirements for the marking of valve components.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>API Specification 6D/ISO 14313:1999
  American Petroleum Institute<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12
Storage and shipping<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.1
Painting<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>All non-corrosion-resistant valves shall be primed and/or painted externally in accordance with the manufacturer’s
standards, unless otherwise agreed, prior to shipment. Stainless-steel valves shall not be painted unless otherwise
agreed. Flange faces, weld bevel ends and exposed stems shall not be painted.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.2
Corrosion prevention<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Prior to shipment, parts and equipment which have bare metallic surfaces shall be protected with a rust preventative
which will provide protection at temperatures up to 50°C (122°F) .<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>12.3
Openings<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Valve flanged and welding ends shall be blanked off to protect the gasket surfaces, welding ends and valve
internals during shipment and storage. Protective covers shall be made of wood, wood fibre, plastic or metal and
shall be securely attached to the valve ends by bolting, steel straps, steel clips or suitable friction-locking devices.
The design of the covers shall prevent the valves from being installed unless the covers have been removed.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Plug, ball and reverse-acting through-conduit gate valves shall be shipped in the fully open position, unless fitted
with a fail-to-close actuator.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Slab-gate valves shall be shipped with the gate in the fully closed position.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Check valves shall be shipped with the disc supported or secured during transit.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Valves provided with stem extensions without an operating mechanism shall have the annular space closed and the
stem extension secured against the outer housing.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>13
Documentation<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The documentation for valves shall include:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   design documentation;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   weld procedure specification (WPS);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   weld procedure qualification record (PQR);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   welder qualification record (WQR);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   qualification records of NDE personnel;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   records of test equipment calibration;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   for valves DN 50 (NPS 2) and larger:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   melt identification certificates for body bonnet/cover(s) and end connector(s) traceable to the unique valve
serial number,<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   serial number for tracing the valve bill of materials,<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   pressure test results.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Documentation shall be provided by the manufacturer in legible, retrievable and reproducible form, and free of
damage.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Documentation required by this International Standard shall be retained by the manufacturer for a minimum of five
years following the date of manufacture.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The purchaser shall specify which particular supplementary documentation requirements in Annex D shall be
provided.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>  American Petroleum Institute
API Specification 6D/ISO 14313:1999<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Annex A
(informative)
Purchasing guidelines<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>A.1 General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This annex provides guidelines to assist the purchaser with valve type selection and specification of specific
requirements when ordering valves.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>A.2 Field testing<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Pressures during the testing of installed valves should not exceed the pressure rating of the valve by more than
50% when testing with the valve partially open or by more than 10% of the pressure rating when testing against a
closed valve.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>NOTE
The maximum test pressure for valves fitted with an external pressure relief may be lower (see 6.8).<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>A.3 Pressure relief<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Certain valve designs will trap pressure in the valve body cavity when the valve is in the fully open and/or closed
position. High internal pressures can result from the thermal expansion of the fluid trapped in these confined areas.
Therefore, if the valve has no self-relieving design provision, pressure relief fittings shall be fitted in the valve body
in accordance with 6.8 of this International Standard.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>A.4 Pigging<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The purchaser should examine the valve design for compatibility with pigging operations when ordering valves for
use in pipelines requiring pigging.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Venturi or reduced-bore valves may not be suitable for pigging operations.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>A valve in which the drive member or the obturator obstructs the bore in the otherwise fully open position (e.g. a
dual-plate check valve) is not piggable.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Certain full-opening valves with pockets may allow bypass of fluid around a short pig or sphere.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>A.5 Fire testing<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The fire resistance design of valves shall be qualified by fire testing in accordance with ISO 10497. Fire resistance
designs already qualified to BS 6755 Part 2, API Spec 6FA, API Spec 6FC, API Spec 6FD or API Std 607, third
edition, are also acceptable.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>A.6 Additional testing<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The purchaser shall specify any additional test requirements not covered by this International Standard.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>A.7 Valve data sheet<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The valve data sheet in this annex may be used to assist with the specification of valves for ordering.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>51<<HEADING_END>>

Supplementary NDE requirements<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>B.1   General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This annex specifies supplementary NDE requirements for the examination of valves which shall be performed by
the manufacturer if specified by the purchaser.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>B.2   Radiographic testing of castings on 100% of critical areas in accordance with
ASME B16.34<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Examination shall be carried out in accordance with ASME Section V, Article 22. The sensitivity, as indicated by
wire penetrometers, shall be 1,5% or better.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Acceptance shall be in accordance with ASME Section VIII, Division 1, Appendix 7. The type and severity level for
acceptance of the welding ends shall be as specified by the purchaser.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>B.3   Radiographic testing of castings on 100% of accessible areas<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Examination shall be carried out in accordance with ASME Section V, Article 22. The sensitivity, as indicated by
wire penetrometers, shall be 1,5% or better.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Acceptance shall be in accordance with ASME Section VIII, Division 1, Appendix 7. The type and severity level for
acceptance of the welding ends shall be as specified by the purchaser.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>B.4   Ultrasonic testing of castings on 100% of critical areas in accordance
with ASME B16.34<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Examination shall be carried out in accordance with ASME Section V, Article 23 using the direct technique or, where
proper access or interpretation of results is not possible, by shear wave examination.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Acceptance shall be in accordance with ASTM A 609, Table 2, Quality Level 1.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>B.5   Ultrasonic testing of castings on 100% of accessible areas<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Examination shall be carried out in accordance with ASME Section V, Article 23 using the direct technique or, where
proper access or interpretation of results is not possible, by shear wave examination.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Acceptance shall be in accordance with ASTM A 609, Table 2, Quality Level 1.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>B.6   Magnetic-particle testing of castings on 100% of surface area<<HEADING_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>  American Petroleum Institute
API Specification 6D/ISO 14313:1999<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>Annex C
(normative)
Supplementary test requirements<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.1   General<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This annex defines requirements for supplementary valve testing which shall be performed by the manufacturer if
specified by the purchaser. The frequency of testing shall also be specified by the purchaser, if not defined in this
annex.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.2   Hydrostatic testing<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>By agreement, hydrostatic testing may be performed at pressures higher than specified in 10.3 and 10.4 and/or for
periods longer than specified in Table 9, 10 or 11.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.3   Low-pressure gas seat testing<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.3.1   Acceptance<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The acceptable leakage rate for low-pressure gas seat testing shall be:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   ISO 5208 Rate A (no visible leakage) for soft-seated valves;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>   ISO 5208 Rate D for metal-seated valves.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.3.2   Type I<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The seat test specified in 10.4 shall be repeated at a test pressure between 0,5 bar and 1,0 bar gauge (7,3 psig and
14,7 psig) using air or nitrogen as the test medium.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.3.3   Type II<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The seat test specified in 10.4 shall be repeated at a test pressure of 5,5  ±  0,7 bar gauge (80,8 psig  ±  10,3 psig)
using air or nitrogen as the test medium.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.4   High-pressure gas testing<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The seat tests specified in 10.2 and 10.4 shall be replaced with a high-pressure seat test using an inert gas as the
test medium. The test pressure and duration shall be as specified in 10.2 and 10.4.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.5   Anti-static testing<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The electrical resistance between the obturator and the valve body and between the stem/shaft and the valve body
shall be measured using a D.C. power source not exceeding 12 V. The resistance shall be measured on dry valves
before pressure testing and shall not exceed 10  Ω .<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>At least 5% of the valves in the order shall be tested.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>57<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>TIPVALVE   Tel:+86-577-88732275  Fax:+86-577-88732276  E-mail:sales@tipvalve.com<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_64>>
<<HEADING level=3>>API Specification 6D/ISO 14313:1999
  American Petroleum Institute<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.6   Torque/thrust testing<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The maximum torque or thrust required to operate ball, gate or plug valves shall be measured at the pressure
specified by the purchaser for the following valve operations:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) open to closed with the bore pressurized and the cavity at atmospheric pressure;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) closed to open with both sides of the obturator pressurized and the cavity at atmospheric pressure;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) closed to open with one side of the obturator pressurized and the cavity at atmospheric pressure;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) as in c) but with the other side of the obturator pressurized.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Torque or thrust values shall be measured with seats free of sealant except where the sealant is the primary means
of  sealing. If necessary for assembly, a lubricant with a viscosity not exceeding that of SAE 10W motor oil or
equivalent may be used.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Thrust and torque testing shall be performed following hydrostatic shell testing and, if specified, low-pressure gas
seat testing.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The measured torque or thrust results shall be compared with the manufacturer’s predicted values.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.7   Cavity relief testing<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.7.1   Frequency<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Each valve shall be tested.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Cavity relief testing is not required if protection of the cavity against over-pressure is ensured, for both the open and
the closed position, by a hole in the obturator or around the seat seal.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.7.2   Trunnion-mounted ball valves and through-conduit gate valves with internal-relieving
seats<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The procedure for cavity relief testing of trunnion-mounted ball valves and through-conduit gate valves with internal-
relieving seats shall be:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) fill the valve in the half-open position with water;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) close the valve and allow water to overflow from the test connection at each end of the valve;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) apply pressure to the valve cavity until one seat relieves the cavity pressure into the valve end and record this
relief pressure;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) for valve types with second-seat relief, continue to increase the pressure to the cavity until the second seat
relieves and record the relief pressure of the second seat.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Failure to relieve shall be cause for rejection.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.7.3   Floating-ball valves<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The procedure for cavity relief testing of floating-ball valves shall be:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) with the valve half-open, pressurize the valve to 1,33 times the valve pressure rating specified in 6.1 for the
material at 38°C (100°F);<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) close the valve and vent each end to atmospheric pressure;<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) open the valve to the half-open position and monitor for the release of test medium trapped in the cavity.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Evidence of trapped pressurizing medium in the cavity shall be cause for rejection.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>58<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>TIPVALVE   Tel:+86-577-88732275  Fax:+86-577-88732276  E-mail:sales@tipvalve.com<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

API Specification 6D/ISO 14313:1999<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>C.8   Hydrogen-induced cracking test<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Process-wetted and pressure-containing parts which are manufactured, fabricated or formed from plate shall be
resistant to hydrogen-induced cracking (HIC). This shall be demonstrated by successful HIC testing in accordance
with NACE TM 0284, except that the test solution shall comply with NACE TM 0177. HIC acceptance criteria, such
as the crack sensitivity ratio (CSR), crack length ratio (CLR) and crack thickness ratio (CTR), shall be specified by
the purchaser.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>ANNEX E
(Informative)<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>API MONOGRAM<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>E.0
Introduction<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The API Monogram Program allows a licensee to apply the API Monogram to products. Products stamped with the
API Monogram provide observable evidence that they were produced in accordance with a verified quality system
and in accordance with an API-recognized, international oil and gas industry product specification. The API
Monogram Program delivers significant value to the international oil and gas industry by linking the verification of a
supplier’s quality system with the demonstrated ability to meet specific product specification requirements.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>When used in conjunction with the requirements of the API License Agreement, API Specification Q1 Parts One
and Two define the program for voluntary licensing of suppliers who wish to provide oil and gas industry products in
accordance with an API-recognized international oil and gas industry product specification.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>API Monogram Program Licenses are issued only after an on-site audit has verified that the licensee conforms with
both the quality system requirements described in API Specification Q1 Part One and the requirements of an API-
recognized international oil and gas industry product specification.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For information on becoming an API Monogram Licensee, please contact API at 1220 L Street, N. W., Washington,
DC 20005 or call 202-682-8000.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>E.1
Scope<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>This Annex sets forth the API Monogram Program requirements necessary for a supplier to consistently produce
products in accordance with API specified requirements<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>E.2
References<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>In addition to the referenced standards listed in Section 2, this Annex references the following standard:<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>API Specification Q1<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>For licensees under the Monogram Program, where cited these requirements are mandatory.  Referenced
standards used by the manufacturer may be either the applicable revision shown in Section 2 and herein, or the
latest revision.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>E.3
API Monogram Program: Licensee responsibilities<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>E.3.1
The requirements for all suppliers desiring to acquire and maintain a license to use the API Monogram shall
include:<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) The quality system requirements of API Specification Q1, Part One.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) The API Monogram Program requirements of API Specification Q1, Part Two.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) The requirements contained in API recognized product specifications.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) The requirements contained in the API License Agreement.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>63<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>TIPVALVE   Tel:+86-577-88732275  Fax:+86-577-88732276  E-mail:sales@tipvalve.com<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PAGE_END>>
<<PAGE_68>>
<<HEADING level=3>>API Specification 6D/ISO 14313:1999
  American Petroleum Institute<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>E.3.2
When a licensed supplier is providing monogrammed product, Parts One and Two of API Specification Q1
are mandatory.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>E.3.3
Each Licensee shall control the application of the monogram in accordance with the following:<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>a) The Licensee shall apply the monogram, license number, and date of manufacture to monogrammed products
in accordance with a marking procedure as specified by the applicable API product specification. Where there
are no API product specification marking requirements, the licensee shall define the location(s) where this
information is applied.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>b) The monogram may be applied at any time appropriate to the manufacturing process but shall be removed if
the product is subsequently found to be in nonconformance with API specified requirements. Products
determined to be nonconforming to API specified requirements shall not bear the API monogram.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>c) Only an API Licensee may apply its monogram.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>d) The monogram shall be applied at the licensed facility.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>e) The authority responsible for applying and removing the API monogram shall be defined.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>E.3.4
Records required by API product specifications shall be retained for the period of time specified therein.
Records specified to demonstrate achievement of the effective operation of the quality system shall be maintained
for a minimum of 5 years.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>E.4
Marking requirements<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>These marking requirements apply only to those API licensees wishing to mark their products with the API
Monogram .<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>E.4.1
Manufacturers shall mark equipment on the nameplate with “API 6D”, in addition to the marking
requirements of Item 15 in Table 12 of Section 11.1.<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>E.4.2
As a minimum, equipment should be marked with English (Imperial) Units.<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>E.4.3
The API Monogram shall be marked on the nameplate, in addition to the marking requirements of Section
11.1.  For valves smaller than DN 50 (NPS 2), the nameplate shall not be omitted, but may be attached to the valve
with stainless steel wire.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>E.5
API Monogram Program: API responsibilities<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The API shall maintain, without references to licensees or users, records of reported problems encountered with
API monogrammed products produced in accordance with API Specification Q1 and API product standards.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>E.6
API Monogram Program: User responsibilities<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The effectiveness of the API monogram program can be strengthened by user reporting problems encountered with
API monogrammed products to the API. API solicits information on both new product nonconformance with API
specified requirements and field failures (or malfunctions) which are judged to be caused by either specification
deficiencies or nonconformance with API specified requirements. Users are requested to report to API problems
encountered with API monogrammed products.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>

<<HEADING level=3>>ANNEX F

<<HEADING level=3>>API REGIONAL ANNEX<<HEADING_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>F.1
Technical Modifications to ISO 14313<<HEADING_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Clause/Subclau se
Modification
6.9
Replace the 1 st  sentence of the 3 rd  paragraph on
page 34 with: "Thread sizes, as a minimum, shall be
in accordance with Table 7, or by agreement."
Explanation
End user may have their own company standard, which deviates from this edition of API
Specification 6D.  This modification allows their use under the specification.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>6.10
Replace the 3 rd  paragraph on page 35 with:
"Wrenches that are of integral design for valves (not
loose), shall not be longer than twice the face-to-
face or end-to-end dimension of the valve, unless
otherwise agreed.”<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Add the following after the 3 rd  paragraph:  “NOTE
Loose wrenches are not considered a part of a valve
and are not required to meet the maximum length
requirements.”
Explanation
This modification brings the wrench paragraph in line with the handwheel paragraph and takes
into account the different operating characteristics of the valve types covered by this
specification and special requests from the purchaser.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>7.1
Replace the 3 rd  paragraph on page 37 with:
“Metallic pressure-containing parts, except stems
and gaskets, shall be made of materials listed in
ASME B16.34 or, by agreement, an equivalent
standard (see clause 6.1).”
Explanation
Clarification of text for manufacturers and purchasers to allow use of an equivalent standard.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<HEADING level=3>>65<<HEADING_END>>

<<PARAGRAPH>>13
Replace the entire clause with:
“Documentation required by this International
Standard shall be maintained by the manufacture for
a minimum of five years following the date of
manufacture.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>- design documentation;
- weld procedure specification (WPS);
- weld procedure qualification record (PQR);
- welder qualification record (WQR);
- qualification records of NDE personnel;
- records of test equipment calibration;
- for valves DN 50 (NPS 2) and larger:
- melt identification certificates for body,
bonnet/cover(s) and end connectors(s)
traceable to the unique valve serial number,
- serial number for tracing the valve bill of
materials,
- pressure test results.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Documentation shall be legible, retrievable, in a
reproducible form, and free of damage.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>The purchaser shall specify which documentation
shall be supplied as listed in Annex D.”<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
<<PARAGRAPH>>Explanation
Clarification of text for manufacturers and purchasers on exactly which documents are required
to be maintained and which type documents are to be provided when requested.<<PARAGRAPH_END>>
